ns go bk">Although this research is already a few weeks old, the tools are still used by ransomware groups and several researcher published since then additionally articles of how to detect and prevent tools like <a class="af nt" href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/edr-bypass-extortion-attempt-thwarted/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">EDRSandBlast</a>. Specifically for the research on top ransomware groups in October 2024 in the context of the Conti affiliate ecosystem, my research has shown that including the other capabilities such groups have, the <a class="af nt" href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/001/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">MITRE ATT&amp;CK technique T1562.001</a> Impair Defenses: Disable or Modify Tools is the most prevalent MITRE ATT&amp;CK technique for 7 out of the top 20 ransomware groups where affiliates from CONTI are still operating since March 2022 in rebranded groups.</p><p id="c140" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mv mw gv mx b my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns go bk">There are many ways to disable or modify security solutions which you can for. e.g qe"></div></div></div></a></div><h1 id="67b5" class="om on gv bf oo op oq or os ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj bk">EDRSandblast</h1><p id="b3f9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mv mw gv mx b my re na nb nc rf ne nf ng rg ni nj nk rh nm nn no ri nq nr ns go bk">EDRSandblast example can be found on github</p><div class="pz qa qb qc qd qe"><a href="https://github.com/wavestone-cdt/EDRSandblast?source=post_page-----d882c290a393--------------------------------" rel="noopener  ugc nofollow" target="_blank"><div class="qf ab iy"><div class="qg ab co cb qh qi"><h2 class="bf gw ip z je qj jg jh qk jj jl gu bk">GitHub - wavestone-cdt/EDRSandblast</h2><div class="ql l"><h3 class="bf b ip z je qj jg jh qk jj jl du">Contribute to VT</p><div class="pz qa qb qc qd qe"><a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/file/d5a1f90dc5c9717b3f900c91a6cdccc20e56e6f1d20f24170189260e8dde7608/relations?source=post_page-----d882c290a393--------------------------------" rel="noopener qk jj jl du">VirusTotal</h3></div><div class="qm l"><p class="bf b dv z je qj jg jh qk jj jl du">VirusTotalwww.virustotal.com</p></div></div></div></a></div><p id="622a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mv mw gv mx b my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns go bk"><strong class="mx gw">Sample hash</strong></p><pre class="nx ny nz oa ob qu qv qw bp qx bb bk"><span id="596e" class="qy on gv qv b bg qz ra l rb rc">d5a1f90dc5c9717b3f900c91a6cdccc20e56e6f1d20f24170189260e8dde7608</span></pre><p id="4e79" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mv mw gv mx b my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns go bk">Executable: DisablerNew.exe (just an example)</p><blockquote class="rw rx ry"><p id="3ae0" class="mv mw rz mx b my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns go bk">EDRSandBlast enumerates the routines defined in those arrays and remove any callback routine linked to a predefined list of EDR drivers (more than 1000 drivers of security products supported, see the <a class="af nt" href="https://github.com/wavestone-cdt/EDRSandblast#edr-drivers-and-processes-detection" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">EDR driver detection section</a>. The enumeration and removal are made possible through the exploitation of an arbitrary Kernel memory read / write primitive provided by the exploitation of a vulnerable driver (see <a class="af nt" href="https://github.com/wavestone-cdt/EDRSandblast#vulnerable-drivers-detection" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Vulnerable drivers section</a>).</p><p id="cbc3" class="mv mw rz mx b my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns go bk">EDRSandblast publicly implements the support of at least 3 vulnerable driver, gdrv.sys (default), RTCore64.sys and DBUtil_2_3.sys. The driver actually used is decided before compilation of the tool (see #define VULN_DRIVER &lt;driver name&gt; in includes/KernelMemoryPrimitive.h). A copy of the vulnerable driver should be downloaded and provided to EDRSandblast for its kernel operation to work.</p><p id="76da" class="mv mw rz mx b my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns go bk">Tested drivers’ hashs are mentionned at the start of each Driver&lt;name&gt;.c file that implements the kernel memory read and write primitives used by EDRSanblast. Using these hashs, drivers samples can be easy found on the Internet, especially on <a class="af nt" href="https://www.loldrivers.io." rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">https://www.loldrivers.io.</a></p></blockquote><h2 id="9aba" class="pk on gv bf oo pl pm dy os pn po ea ow ng pp pq pr nk ps pt pu no pv pw px py bk"><strong class="al">Supported gw">CVE-2024–1853</strong></p><blockquote class="rw rx ry"><p id="6eb1" class="mv mw rz mx b my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns go bk">CVE-2024–1853 is an Arbitrary Process Termination vulnerability identified in Zemana AntiLogger v2.74.204.664. This vulnerability exploits the 0x80002048 IOCTL code of the Zemana AntiLogger drivers, allowing an attacker to terminate processes arbitrarily, including critical security processes such as AV or EDR software.</p><p id="6b18" class="mv mw rz mx b my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns go bk">In May 2023, a threat actor with the pseudonym “SpyBoy” incorporated this vulnerability into a tool named “Terminator,” marketed as an “EDR killer” tool. Terminator leverages CVE-2024–1853 by using the vulnerable Zemana AntiLogger driver to disable security solutions on targeted systems. SpyBoy promoted and sold this tool on Russian hacking forums, offering it for prices ranging from $300 for specific AV bypasses to $3000 for an all-in-one solution.</p><p id="98ab" class="mv mw rz mx b my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns go bk">Killer Ultra is packed with the Zemana driver <strong class="mx gw">“amsdk.sys”</strong> which is automatically extracted and written to disk in the execution directory of Killer Ultra as a file named <strong class="mx gw">“trevor”.</strong></p></blockquote><p id="6fbf" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mv mw gv mx b my mz na nb
